
CREATE OR REPLACE TABLE WAREHOUSE_JAM_DATA (
    SITE_NAME VARCHAR(10) PRIMARY KEY,
    WAREHOUSE_LOCATION VARCHAR(50),
    CAPACITY NUMBER,
    GENERATION_TYPE VARCHAR(10),
    SISTER_SITE VARCHAR(3),
    RETROFIT_STATUS VARCHAR(10),
    EQUIPMENT_TYPE VARCHAR(50),
    JAM_COUNT NUMBER,
    DOWNTIME_HOURS NUMBER(10,2),
    LOSS_PREVENTION_HOURS NUMBER(10,2),
    COST_OF_JAMS NUMBER,
    MAINTENANCE_INTERVENTION NUMBER,
    AUTOMATION_LEVEL VARCHAR(10),
    AVERAGE_THROUGHPUT NUMBER,
    PEAK_HOURS VARCHAR(20),
    REGION VARCHAR(50),
    PRIMARY_CARRIER VARCHAR(50),
    WEATHER_IMPACT VARCHAR(3),
    VENDOR VARCHAR(50),
    YEAR_BUILT NUMBER(4)
);

SELECT * FROM WAREHOUSE_JAM_DATA;






-- rename the table 
ALTER TABLE WAREHOUSE_JAM_DATA
RENAME TO warehouse;


--- Checking out the data:
SELECT * FROM warehouse 
WHERE retrofit_status = 'FULL' OR jam_count >= 350;


SELECT generation_type, jam_count, downtime_hours, equipment_type
FROM warehouse
WHERE equipment_type <> 'Sorter';


ALTER TABLE warehouse
RENAME COLUMN LOSS_PREVENTION_HOURS TO LPH;



SELECT *
FROM warehouse
WHERE retrofit_status LIKE 'Partial%';


SELECT *
FROM warehouse
WHERE warehouse_location IN ('Japan', 'Germany', 'USA');



SELECT *
FROM warehouse
WHERE year_built >= 1990 AND year_built <=2000;



SELECT *
FROM warehouse
WHERE peak_hours IS NULL;


SELECT * FROM warehouse 
WHERE year_built <=2000
AND ( COST_OF_JAMS >=20000  OR  AVERAGE_THROUGHPUT >=5000);



SELECT * FROM warehouse
ORDER BY jam_count DESC;




SELECT site_name, warehouse_location, capacity, generation_type, jam_count, average_throughput, equipment_type
FROM warehouse 
ORDER BY capacity DESC;

SELECT region,
       COUNT(*) AS count
  FROM warehouse
 GROUP BY region;

-- 
SELECT retrofit_status,
       COUNT(*) AS count
  FROM warehouse
 GROUP BY retrofit_status;

---

SELECT warehouse_location,
       retrofit_status,
       COUNT(*) AS count
  FROM warehouse
 GROUP BY warehouse_location, retrofit_status
 order by retrofit_status, warehouse_location;

---



SELECT DISTINCT Vendor FROM warehouse; 

--- sites that are older have more MHE problems and need to be monitored on a list to ensure they are running well. We can do checks on these sites with out SME's.

SELECT year_built FROM warehouse
GROUP BY year_built;


--- Analysis to identify the warehouse country and count for each retrofit status and order by the retrofit status (full, none,partial) with jam count over 235
SELECT warehouse_location,
       retrofit_status,
       COUNT(*) AS count
  FROM warehouse
 GROUP BY warehouse_location, retrofit_status
 HAVING MAX(jam_count) > 235
 order by retrofit_status, warehouse_location;





---- chaging the data (column name)

ALTER TABLE warehouse
RENAME COLUMN MAINTENANCE_INTERVENTION TO freq_of_maintenance_a_week;

ALTER TABLE warehouse
RENAME COLUMN downtime_hours TO DTH;

ALTER TABLE warehouse
RENAME COLUMN jam_count TO faulted_occurances;

ALTER TABLE warehouse
RENAME COLUMN faulted_occurances TO faulted_occurances_daily;

ALTER TABLE warehouse
RENAME COLUMN DTH TO DTH_a_week;

ALTER TABLE warehouse
RENAME COLUMN LPH TO LPH_a_week;

SELECT * FROM warehouse;




---Identify the warehouse country and count for each retrofit status and order by the retrofit status (full, none,partial) with 
---LPH between 0 and 50 (to see if the retrofits are benefical to the overall lower LPH int he network) 
---results are 34 for full, 33 for none, 35 for partial


SELECT warehouse_location,
       retrofit_status,
       COUNT(*) AS count
  FROM warehouse
 GROUP BY warehouse_location, retrofit_status
 HAVING COUNT(LPH_a_week) BETWEEN 0 AND 50
 order by retrofit_status, warehouse_location;




-- Add columns and make it a set of values
ALTER TABLE warehouse 
ADD TOP_FAULTED_EQUIP VARCHAR(10)


ALTER TABLE warehouse 
ADD main_cost NUMBER(10)

UPDATE warehouse
SET main_cost = ROUND(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(10000, 100000), 2);



SELECT column_name 
FROM all_tab_columns 
WHERE table_name = 'warehouse';

ALTER TABLE warehouse
RENAME COLUMN main_cost TO cost_of_retrofit;

--- Populating the tables further

SELECT 
    cost_of_retrofit,
    automation_level,
    retrofit_status,
    CASE 
        WHEN automation_level = 'High' AND retrofit_status = 'Partial' THEN cost_of_retrofit * 1.6
        WHEN automation_level = 'Medium' AND retrofit_status = 'Partial' THEN cost_of_retrofit * 1.2
        WHEN automation_level = 'Low' AND retrofit_status = 'Partial' THEN cost_of_retrofit * 1.1
        WHEN automation_level = 'High' AND retrofit_status = 'Full' THEN cost_of_retrofit * 2.2
        WHEN automation_level = 'Medium' AND retrofit_status = 'Full' THEN cost_of_retrofit * 1.8
        WHEN automation_level = 'Low' AND retrofit_status = 'Full' THEN cost_of_retrofit * 1.5
        ELSE cost_of_retrofit
    END AS adjusted_retrofit_cost
FROM warehouse;

UPDATE warehouse
SET cost_of_retrofit = 
    CASE
        WHEN automation_level = 'High' AND retrofit_status = 'Partial' THEN cost_of_retrofit * 1.6
        WHEN automation_level = 'Medium' AND retrofit_status = 'Partial' THEN cost_of_retrofit * 1.2
        WHEN automation_level = 'Low' AND retrofit_status = 'Partial' THEN cost_of_retrofit * 1.1
        WHEN automation_level = 'High' AND retrofit_status = 'Full' THEN cost_of_retrofit * 2.2
        WHEN automation_level = 'Medium' AND retrofit_status = 'Full' THEN cost_of_retrofit * 1.8
        WHEN automation_level = 'Low' AND retrofit_status = 'Full' THEN cost_of_retrofit * 1.5
    END;





    SELECT 
    SITE_NAME, 
    COST_OF_JAMS, 
    FAULTED_OCCURANCES_DAILY,
    CASE 
        WHEN COST_OF_JAMS > 10000 AND FAULTED_OCCURANCES_DAILY > 10 THEN 'Critical Jam Costs'
        WHEN COST_OF_JAMS BETWEEN 5000 AND 10000 THEN 'Manageable Jam Costs'
        ELSE 'Low Jam Costs'
    END AS Jam_Cost_Impact
FROM warehouse;



-- since this column can be useful, I will add it to the table with the conditions below (ADD COLUMN THEN SET COLUMN)
ALTER TABLE warehouse
ADD jam_impact VARCHAR(50);

UPDATE warehouse 
SET jam_impact = 
    CASE 
        WHEN COST_OF_JAMS > 10000 AND FAULTED_OCCURANCES_DAILY > 10 THEN 'Critical Jam Costs'
        WHEN COST_OF_JAMS BETWEEN 5000 AND 10000 THEN 'Manageable Jam Costs'
        ELSE 'Low Jam Costs'
    END;

    SELECT * FROM warehouse; 

-- we can use this data to prioritize the critical jam costs buildings 
SELECT site_name, warehouse_location, Generation_type, retrofit_status, equipment_type, automation_level,vendor
FROM warehouse 
WHERE jam_impact = 'Critical Jam Costs';






SELECT 
    SITE_NAME, 
    YEAR_BUILT, 
    COST_OF_RETROFIT,
    CASE 
        WHEN YEAR_BUILT < 1980 THEN COST_OF_RETROFIT * 1.5
        WHEN YEAR_BUILT BETWEEN 1980 AND 2000 THEN COST_OF_RETROFIT * 1.2
        ELSE COST_OF_RETROFIT
    END AS Forecasted_Retrofit_Cost
FROM warehouse;




-- rename a duplicate value in a column
UPDATE warehouse
SET GENERATION_TYPE = 'Gen9'
WHERE GENERATION_TYPE = 'Gen13';




/*
change the automation level of the buildings for data accuracy
for this example I wanted all Gen 11 buildings to be high automation, for the next example all Gen 10 will be medium and 
Gen 12 will be highest, Gen 9 will be lowest (after I rename the Gen 13 to Gen 9 */
SELECT GENERATION_TYPE, 
COUNT(*) AS count
FROM warehouse
GROUP BY GENERATION_TYPE;

UPDATE warehouse
SET AUTOMATION_LEVEL = 'Lowest'
WHERE GENERATION_TYPE = 'Gen9';

UPDATE warehouse
SET AUTOMATION_LEVEL = 'Low'
WHERE GENERATION_TYPE = 'Gen10';

UPDATE warehouse
SET AUTOMATION_LEVEL = 'Medium'
WHERE GENERATION_TYPE = 'Gen11';

UPDATE warehouse
SET AUTOMATION_LEVEL = 'Highest'
WHERE GENERATION_TYPE = 'Gen12';

SELECT GENERATION_TYPE, AUTOMATION_LEVEL FROM warehouse;

UPDATE warehouse
SET cost_of_retrofit = NULL
WHERE retrofit_status = 'None';

SELECT w.site_name, w.warehouse_location, r.repair_type_name, r.description, r.repair_cost
FROM warehouse w   --The alias for the table warehouse
INNER JOIN repair_types r  -- the alias for the table repair_types
ON w.repair_type_id = r.repair_type_id;   -- the connecting key for the tables (warehouse & repair_types)
--This query will show site_name, warehouse_location, and corresponding repair details such as repair_type_name, description, and repair_cost.



-- we need to make the repair type null for the retrofits that are none

UPDATE repair_types
SET repair_type_name = 'None',
    description = 'None',
    repair_cost = 0
WHERE repair_type_name = 'Cooling System Repair';

SELECT * FROM repair_types;

SET repair_type_id = 11
WHERE retrofit_status = 'None';

SELECT w.site_name, w.warehouse_location, r.repair_type_name, r.description
FROM warehouse w
LEFT JOIN repair_types r
ON w.repair_type_id = r.repair_type_id  -- the connecting key for the tables (warehouse & repair_types)
WHERE r.repair_type_name = 'None';

SELECT SUM(repair_cost) FROM repair_types;



-- calculate the total repair costs per region
SELECT w.region, SUM(r.repair_cost) AS total_repair_cost -- This query calculates the total repair costs for each region by summing the repair_cost values.
FROM warehouse w
INNER JOIN repair_types r
ON w.repair_type_id = r.repair_type_id -- the connecting key for the tables (warehouse & repair_types)
GROUP BY w.region;



--- filter repairs based on the costs greater than 500,000
SELECT w.site_name, r.repair_type_name, r.repair_cost
FROM warehouse w
INNER JOIN repair_types r
ON w.repair_type_id = r.repair_type_id
WHERE r.repair_cost > 500000;



-- this data doesnt bring actionable insights since it isnt accurate (all emergency repairs would cost the most and our data doesnt reflect that) Eventually we will fix it later in the notes



SELECT w.site_name AS site_name,
       r.repair_type_name AS repair_type,
       r.repair_cost AS repair_cost,
       w.FAULTED_OCCURANCES_DAILY AS faulted_occurances
  FROM warehouse w
  LEFT JOIN repair_types r
    ON w.repair_type_id = r.repair_type_id

---- the left join below, its the same as doing a right join with switching the table names


  SELECT w.site_name AS site_name,
       r.repair_type_name AS repair_type,
       r.repair_cost AS repair_cost,
       w.FAULTED_OCCURANCES_DAILY AS faulted_occurances
  FROM repair_types r
  LEFT JOIN warehouse w
    ON w.repair_type_id = r.repair_type_id
    ORDER BY FAULTED_OCCURANCES_DAILY




--- work on the data accuracy in jams equations
	ALTER TABLE warehouse
	RENAME COLUMN  lph_a_week TO lph

	UPDATE warehouse
	SET LPH = 25.99;

	UPDATE warehouse
	SET cost_of_jams = FAULTED_OCCURANCES_DAILY * LPH;
---

----- join tables with some columns and repair costs > 5000,order by repair costs


SELECT w.site_name AS site_name,
	       w.generation_type AS gen_type,
	       r.repair_type_name AS repair_type,
	       r.repair_cost AS repair_cost,
	       w.FAULTED_OCCURANCES_DAILY AS faulted_occurances,
	       w.cost_of_jams AS jam_costs,
	       w.automation_level AS automation
	FROM repair_types r
	LEFT JOIN warehouse w
	    ON w.repair_type_id = r.repair_type_id
	    AND repair_cost > 50000
	    ORDER BY repair_cost DESC


-- join tables with some columns, cost of jams > repair costs and ordered by faulted occurances daily


SELECT w.site_name AS site_name,
	       w.generation_type AS gen_type,
	       w.FAULTED_OCCURANCES_DAILY AS faulted_occurances,
	       w.cost_of_jams AS jam_costs,
	       r.repair_type_name AS repair_type,
	       r.repair_cost AS repair_cost
	FROM repair_types r
	LEFT JOIN warehouse w
	    ON w.repair_type_id = r.repair_type_id
	    AND w.cost_of_jams > r.repair_cost 
	    ORDER BY FAULTED_OCCURANCES_DAILY 


-- weather table full join
SELECT * FROM weather_disruptions;


SELECT 
	 w.*, -- Select all columns from the warehouse table
	 wd.*  -- Select all columns from the repair_types table
FROM warehouse w
FULL OUTER JOIN weather_disruptions wd
ON w.weather_impact = wd.weather_impact;



-- working on data accuracy again
SELECT DISTINCT region FROM warehouse;

	-- updating lph based on regions
UPDATE warehouse
SET LPH = CASE 
	          WHEN region = 'Europe' THEN 28.99
	          WHEN region = 'Asia-Pacific' THEN 15.50
	          WHEN region = 'North America' THEN 30.25
	          ELSE LPH -- Keeps the current value if region doesn't match any condition
END;



SELECT  DISTINCT GENERATION_TYPE
FROM warehouse;





-- update the capacity and faulted occurances based on generation type
UPDATE warehouse
SET capacity = CASE 
	            WHEN GENERATION_TYPE = 'Gen9' THEN ROUND(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(400000, 500000), 2) -- Between 400K and 500K
	            WHEN GENERATION_TYPE = 'Gen10' THEN ROUND(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(600000, 800000), 2) -- Between 600K and 800K
	            WHEN GENERATION_TYPE = 'Gen11' THEN ROUND(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(900000, 1100000), 2) -- Between 900K and 1.1M
	            WHEN GENERATION_TYPE = 'Gen12' THEN ROUND(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(1200000, 1700000), 2) -- Between 1.2M and 1.7M
	            ELSE capacity -- Keeps the current value if GENERATION_TYPE doesn't match
	          END;



-- updating the year built based on the generation type
UPDATE warehouse
SET year_built = CASE 
	            WHEN generation_type = 'Gen9' THEN ROUND(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(1990, 2000), 0)
	            WHEN generation_type = 'Gen10' THEN ROUND(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(2001, 2010), 0)
	            WHEN generation_type = 'Gen11' THEN ROUND(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(2011, 2019), 0)
	            WHEN generation_type = 'Gen12' THEN ROUND(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(2020, 2025), 0)
	            ELSE LPH -- Keeps the current value if year_built doesn't match any condition
	          END;


---Updating the cost of jams based on LPH

UPDATE warehouse
	SET cost_of_jams = FAULTED_OCCURANCES_DAILY * LPH


CREATE TABLE jams (
    site_id VARCHAR2(5) PRIMARY KEY,
    daily_jams NUMBER,
    dth DECIMAL(2,2),
    loss_prevention_hours DECIMAL(2,2),
    jam_costs NUMBER,
    maintenance_hours NUMBER
);




INSERT INTO jams (site_id)
SELECT w.site_name
FROM warehouse w;


UPDATE jams
SET daily_jams = TRUNC(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(1, 200));


UPDATE jams
SET jam_costs = TRUNC(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(500, 10000));

UPDATE jams
SET maintenance_hours = TRUNC(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(1, 60));

SELECT * FROM jams;

-- modify the datatype of a variable from a table :
ALTER TABLE jams
MODIFY dth DECIMAL(4,2); -- Allows values up to 999.99

UPDATE jams
SET dth = ROUND(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(0.10, 29.99), 2);

UPDATE warehouse
SET AVERAGE_THROUGHPUT = CASE 
	WHEN GENERATION_TYPE = 'Gen9' THEN ROUND(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(400000, 500000), 2) -- Between 400K and 500K
	WHEN GENERATION_TYPE = 'Gen10' THEN ROUND(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(600000, 800000), 2) -- Between 600K and 800K
	WHEN GENERATION_TYPE = 'Gen11' THEN ROUND(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(900000, 1100000), 2) -- Between 900K and 1.1M
	WHEN GENERATION_TYPE = 'Gen12' THEN ROUND(DBMS_RANDOM.VALUE(1200000, 1700000), 2) -- Between 1.2M and 1.7M
ELSE AVERAGE_THROUGHPUT -- Keeps the current value if GENERATION_TYPE doesn't match
END;
